Construction of the Ministry of Communications New Building 48

(Nanjing) The new building of the Ministry of Communications has been completed and has been fully moved into for office work. Regarding the construction process, the reporter learned from the new building of the ministry that it was designed and supervised by architect Yue Long, and Shanghai Xin Feng Ji was the contractor. Construction began on July 20 of the 19th year of the Republic. It was interrupted for a long time due to the major floods of the 20th year of the Republic and the "September 18th" and "January 28th" incidents. When Zhu Jiahua took over the ministry the year before last, there was a proposal to stop construction during the national crisis. After consultation with the architect and research by lawyers, it was said that a contract had been signed, and the construction had been going on for two and a half years. There was no reason to abandon it halfway in law or in fact. Moreover, it was found that the contract price was agreed to be paid in eight installments. Because the payments were made on time, six installments had been paid by the time of the suspension of work. Only two installments remained, but the project had been suspended for a long time due to various reasons, and only 20% had been completed. The price paid had greatly exceeded the value of the project, and it was impossible to terminate the contract. Therefore, it was only possible to urge Xin Feng Ji to continue the project as soon as possible according to the original plan, so as to complete it as soon as possible. It was interrupted several times due to the strike of two people, and it has only been completed to this day. The reasons for the delay are mainly due to the contractor's insufficient capital, poor performance, and other unexpected events. As for the auxiliary construction and interior equipment, efforts have been made to save money. For example, the eight electric elevators originally planned have not been installed. Even the furniture currently used in the entire building, except for the auditorium and one or two reception rooms, is all original and has only been repainted. In addition, the Post Office Headquarters, the Postal Savings Headquarters, and the Long-Distance Telephone Engineering Office of the nine provinces were all located separately in the past, and the expenses were very large. In the future, joint offices will be established, and expenses can be saved, and administrative efficiency will also be improved. (Central News Agency Dispatch, 26th)

Shanghai factories are competing to buy Xuzhou tobacco leaves, and the supply is less than the demand. Some are even shipped to the United States. However, this year's production is only more than 200,000 packages, and there are few left now. This is an unprecedentedly good situation. Central Antiquities Preservation Committee Member Teng Gu and Others Returned to Beijing Yesterday 64

Having Completed the Inspection of Historical Sites in Henan and Shaanxi

(Nanjing) Central Antiquities Preservation Committee members Teng Gu and Huang Wenbi have completed their inspection of historical sites in Henan and Shaanxi provinces and returned to Beijing on the 26th. According to their account, they first went to Bian, then went from Zheng to Zhangde to inspect the ancient capital of the Yin Dynasty and the stone caves of the Northern Wei and Sui Tang Dynasties. The sculptures are exquisite, but many Buddha heads have been cut off by treacherous merchants colluding with local people. Then they went to Luoyang to inspect the ruins of Jin Yong City, the ruins of the Han Dynasty Imperial Academy, and the White Horse Temple and Longmen Grottoes. Although they are gradually becoming dilapidated and half of them are in ruins, the past prosperity of the cultural relics is still admirable. Finally, they went to Xi'an and traveled through Xianyang, Xingping, Lintong, and other counties to inspect the ancient tombs of the Zhou, Qin, and Han dynasties and the ancient temples of the Sui and Tang dynasties. They will discuss with the provincial government to protect the ancient sculptures that have been neglected in the past. Historical sites are scattered throughout Henan and Shaanxi provinces, which makes people nostalgic for the great creations of their predecessors. They will draft a detailed report within a few days and propose concrete measures to the Executive Yuan. (Central News Agency Dispatch, 26th)

Three Major Constructions in Hubei Province 93

Highways Completed: 2,600 Li

Telephone Service Connects 51 Bureaus

Excellent Business After Government Took Over Navigation Administration

Hankou Dispatch: Hubei Province has suffered from frequent disasters in recent years, leaving no time to save the dying, let alone speak of construction. However, due to bandit suppression and work-for-relief projects, many highways and telephone lines have been completed, and inland river navigation has also been effectively rectified. The following is a record of the three major constructions: highways, telephones, and navigation administration.

Highways 94

The construction of highways in Hubei Province is managed by the Mountain Construction Department. The so-called Bian-Yue, Jing-Chuan, and Luo-Shao three major trunk lines, which traverse the province, were planned by the National Economic Council. The rest are either connecting lines, secondary lines, or county roads, totaling twenty-six. They are: (1) From Hankou via Songbu, Huangpi, Macheng to Xiaojieling, 181 kilometers long; (2) From Wuchang to Ge Dian, 32 kilometers long; (3) From Daye to Yangxin, 6 kilometers long; (4) From Guangji to Xishui, 56 kilometers long; (5) From Hankou via Changjiangbu, Yingcheng, Zaoshi, Shatan, Shilipu, Dangyang to Yichang, 360 kilometers long; (6) From Laohekou via Fancheng, Xiangyang, Yicheng, Jingmen, Jiangling to Shashi, 281 kilometers long; (7) From Shashi to Gong'an, 79 kilometers long; (8) From Fancheng via Zaoyang, Suixian, Anlu to Huayuan, 333 kilometers long; (9) From Laohekou via Gucheng, Caodian, Junxian, Tuyan, Yunxian to Baihe, 272 kilometers long; (10) From Yicheng via Wu'an to Nanzhang, 50 kilometers long; (11) From Zhongxiang via Jingshan, Zaoshi, Tianmen to Yuekou, 190 kilometers long; (12) From Anlu via Yunmeng to Changjiangbu, 52 kilometers long; (13) From Guangshui via Lishan to Huangpi, 116 kilometers long; (14) From Songbu via Huang'an to Huayuan, 150 kilometers long; (15) From Zhongguan Station to Zhongtu Store, 45 kilometers long; (16) From Guangji to Wuxue, 36 kilometers long; (17) From Yangjiaze via Jiukou, Zhongxiang, Fengle River to Kuaihuopu, 140 kilometers long; (18) From Daye to Huangshigang, 35 kilometers long; (19) From Yingcheng via Yunmeng to Xiaogan, 80 kilometers long; (20) From Yingcheng to Tiandian, 23 kilometers long; (21) From Yingcheng to Chenjiahe, 18 kilometers long; (22) From Yingcheng to Linhekou, 10 kilometers long; (23) From Wuchang to Qingshan, 18 kilometers long; (24) From Wuchang to Jinkou, 35 kilometers long; (25) From Wuchang to Luojia Mountain, 16 kilometers long; (26) From Wuchang to Baiju, 58 kilometers long. The total length of highways in the province is 2,695 kilometers. The total daily car travel distance is 6,000 kilometers. The newly built Gan-E trunk line, from Wuchang directly to Nanchang, will be completed by the end of the year.

Telephone 95

The province's long-distance telephone lines are installed along the highways. Telephone sub-bureaus are set up in fifty-one locations, including Huayuan, Wushengguan, Hengdian, Xinjia Po, Anlu, Wuxue, Huangpi, Changjiangbu, Suixian, Guangji, Cangzibu, Yingcheng, Shayang, Xiaogan, Zaoyang, Xishui, Songbu, Zaoshi, Fancheng, Yingshan, Macheng, Luotian, Huangtugang, Guangshui, Tuan Po, Futian River, Tuanfeng, Laohekou, Yunmeng, Gucheng, Yunxian, Junxian, Baihe, Baokang, Fangxian, Zhushan, Shihua Street, Yicheng, Lihe Linshan, Xin Zhou, Xiaojieling, Huang'an, Yuekou, Tianmen, Yangjiaze, Tangchi, Songhe, Tiandian, and Shiyan Caodian. Eastern Hubei, Central Hubei, and Northern Hubei have all been connected by telephone, totaling 2,520 kilometers. However, the counties in Southern Hubei, although they have been installed, have been destroyed by bandits and are currently being planned for reconstruction.

Navigation Administration 96

The province's navigation affairs, apart from the Wuhan Ferry, which has five ferry lines and twelve upper and lower docks, carrying 50,000 passengers daily and generating 40,000 yuan in monthly income and is directly managed by the Construction Department, the other inland river navigation, eastward to Wuxue, westward to Yichang, southward into Hunan, and northward to Xiangfan, are all controlled by shipping merchants. In the spring of this year, the Fuyuan and Huitong ships and others successively had accidents, drowning 2,000 passengers. The Provincial Government then ordered the Construction Department to manage and operate on their behalf. A total of ninety small vessels from various companies, those that were not damaged, fifty-seven steamships, and nineteen diesel ships, were allocated to run on twenty-one routes. There are eleven important routes: (1) From Hankou to Wuxue, 214 kilometers long; (2) From Hankou to Cangzibu, 65 kilometers long; (3) From Hankou to Liuzhi Store, 63 kilometers long; (4) From Hankou to Shashi, 519 kilometers long; (5) From Hankou to Zhuhe, 193 kilometers long; (6) From Hankou to Maojiakou, 240 kilometers long; (7) From Hankou to Pengjiachang, 135 kilometers long; (8) From Hankou to Shayang, 297 kilometers long; (9) From Hankou to Changjiangbu, 111 kilometers long; (10) From Hankou to Tianmen, 183 kilometers long; (11) From Shashi to Yichang, 137 kilometers long, totaling 2,153 kilometers. There are over one hundred docks, carrying over 6,000 passengers daily, with monthly revenue ranging from 70,000 to 100,000 yuan. However, the reorganization period is limited to one year. Next March, it will be completed. Whether it will still be controlled by the government or returned to commercial management is still unknown. (25th)

The Ministry of Finance's Review of the Past and Future of National Fiscal Reorganization 97

Over 30 Million Yuan Worth of Excessive Taxes and Miscellaneous Levies Abolished in Various Provinces

The Crucial Policies of Land Registration and County Budget Preparation Are Currently Underway

Beijing Dispatch: Minister of Finance Kong Xiangxi, recognizing the decline of China's economy and the bankruptcy of the rural areas in recent years, and deeply feeling the hardship of the local people's poverty and financial exhaustion while reorganizing the national economy, proposed two resolutions during the Fourth Plenary Session of the Fourth Central Executive Committee in February of the 23rd year of the Republic: reorganizing national land taxes, first conducting land registration, and reducing land tax surcharges to provide relief to rural areas. The General Assembly passed the principles and the National Government ordered the Executive Yuan to issue three methods for reducing land tax surcharges and abolishing excessive taxes and miscellaneous levies, which were reported to the Ministry within the deadline, so that when convening the National Finance Conference, the financial authorities and expert members of various provinces and cities could earnestly explore compensation methods and agree on the types and scope of local taxes in order to determine concrete measures. Subsequently, the National Finance Conference opened, with a total of 193 representatives from various places attending, and as many as 127 proposals were made. Apart from the (1) Reorganization of Local Finance Case, (2) Land Registration Case, and (3) Reduction of Land Tax Surcharges in Various Provinces, with Deficiencies to be Supplemented by the Central Government, which were discussed by the Finance Committee, there were 25 cases related to the reorganization of land taxes and reduction of surcharges, 34 cases related to improving the tax system and abolishing excessive taxes and miscellaneous levies, 36 cases related to determining local budgets, and 39 cases related to other items such as rectifying the currency system and providing financial relief. After seven days of deliberation, concrete plans were agreed upon for conducting land registration, reducing land tax surcharges, abolishing excessive taxes and miscellaneous levies, and reorganizing various local finances, and a Reorganization of Local Taxes and Miscellaneous Levies Committee was established within the Ministry, with supervisory committees established in various provinces and cities to enhance effectiveness. Subsequently, the National Government issued a clear order on June 8, stipulating that no further land tax surcharges should be added forever, and no illegal taxes and levies should be established again forever. On the 25th of the same month, it further issued a clear order specifying six categories of illegal taxes and levies and four stages of reorganization, all of which were forwarded by Minister of Finance Kong Xiangxi to all provinces and cities for uniform compliance, all of which were the principles determined to reduce the burden on the people after the Fourth Plenary Session of the Fourth Central Executive Committee, and also the concrete measures formulated to reduce the burden on the people after the Second National Finance Conference.

After the abolition of yellow taxes and miscellaneous levies and the reduction of land tax surcharges, local expenses would be insufficient, and without the central government's prior planning to supplement them, they would inevitably be inadequate. The most noteworthy of these is the issue of compensation. However, the central government's finances are also not abundant, but the central government and local governments are originally one entity. Within the possible scope, no matter how difficult it may be, we must find ways to consider the local situation. Therefore, Minister Kong allocated a portion of the national tax revenue to supplement local finances at a time when the central government's finances were extremely difficult, so as to avoid the fact that the decision could not be implemented due to lack of compensation. For example, the tobacco and alcohol license tax was entirely assigned to the provinces and cities to take over and collect at the beginning of the current fiscal year for compensation. In addition, the stamp tax was originally a central government tax, but after submitting a plan to the Executive Yuan for approval, it was decided to allocate a portion of it for compensation, with the Ministry collecting and distributing it, allocating 10% to the provinces, 30% to the counties, and 20% to supplement remote and impoverished provinces, and changing it to be sold by post offices to eliminate the previous abuses of contracting and apportioning. Reinspection methods were also stipulated to prevent missed postings. If handled properly, local funds in the future will inevitably become more abundant. In addition, the Ministry of Finance also sacrificed approximately 2 million yuan in revenue from the national treasury each year to abolish the parcel transit tax as an initiative for local areas to abolish excessive taxes and miscellaneous levies.

In order to uphold the late Premier's legacy of relieving the suffering of the people and seeking its thorough implementation, the Ministry of Finance has repeatedly issued and urged all provinces and cities to uniformly comply with the above resolutions. In the months since then, various provinces and cities have successively reported the abolition of excessive taxes and miscellaneous levies and land tax surcharges, including Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Jiangxi, Hunan, Hubei, Fujian, Guangdong, Henan, Shandong, Hebei, Shanxi, Shaanxi, Ningxia, Chahar, Gansu, Suiyuan, Guizhou, Qinghai, Guangxi, Yunnan, Beiping, and Weihaiwei, a total of 23 provinces and cities, abolishing approximately over 3,000 types of taxes. The amount of taxes already abolished totaled over 28 million yuan, and those about to be abolished amounted to 9 million yuan, totaling over 30 million yuan. The 30 million yuan in tax revenue abolished were all the blood and sweat of the people, as well as all the burdens of the people. However, the Ministry of Finance authorities believe that China has a vast territory and many types of taxes, and there are still many that have not been reduced. Therefore, they are still encouraging each other with local authorities to continue to move forward, allowing no trivial details to remain and ensuring that no one is deprived.

As for the long-standing abuses of land tax in our country, which are deeply rooted, the reorganization of land cannot be delayed. The late Premier said, "If the land problem is solved, the Principle of People's Livelihood can be solved." However, the implementation of national land measurement and equalization of land rights cannot be done in a short time. Therefore, the Ministry of Finance, based on the principles agreed upon at the Fourth Plenary Session of the Fourth Central Executive Committee, first conducted land registration, formulated a 35-article outline, and submitted it to the Executive Yuan for approval for all provinces and cities to prepare for implementation. At present, Jiangsu, Anhui, Hubei, Hunan, Fujian, Hebei, Henan, Shaanxi, Shanxi, Guizhou, Suiyuan, Shandong, Sichuan, and Qinghai provinces have already begun preparations.

Annual meetings and monthly summaries are a constant part of the national economy. Without a budget, there is no way to find any trace of fiscal order. In the past, local budgets were either not established due to unrest or because government orders were not able to be universally applied, and the budgets of various counties were even more unfounded. After this finance conference, all provinces also ordered counties to implement the preparation of budgets. At present, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Hebei, Shaanxi, Shandong, Anhui, Guizhou, Hubei, Hunan, Gansu, Chahar, and Suiyuan provinces have begun to prepare county budgets, and the four provinces of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Shaanxi, and Hebei have also convened small group meetings of county magistrates to actively carry out the work, which has achieved considerable results. Other items such as reorganizing various legal taxes and levies, reforming the land tax collection system, unifying accounting, and reorganizing debt payments, although the situations in various provinces are different and not entirely the same, are also gradually being improved according to local conditions. The following is an appendix to the general outline of the reorganization of various provinces for the reference of those who care about China's finance.

Jiangsu Province: Jiangsu has always been known for its wealth. Before the ninth year of the Republic, revenue and expenditure could still be offset. After the 13th year of the Republic, military affairs were frequent, military salaries and taxes were heavy, debts increased daily, budgets gradually fell short, and the finances of various counties were insufficient, and funds were raised at any time due to events. Land tax surcharges and excessive taxes and miscellaneous levies increased at any time. After the Second National Finance Conference closed, various resolutions were implemented. Regarding the abolition of excessive taxes and miscellaneous levies, the first batch of tax cuts amounted to 100,174 yuan, the second batch 132,707 yuan, and the third batch 95,521 yuan, totaling 328,402 yuan. Regarding the reduction of land tax surcharges, there were five counties including Yixing, totaling 137,976 yuan. Regarding the determination of budgets, 3,040,000 yuan was cut.

Zhejiang Province: Zhejiang Province is also a wealthy area in the southeast. Before the tenth year of the Republic, revenue and expenditure could barely be balanced. After the 13th year of the Republic, wars broke out repeatedly, gradually losing the balance. As of the end of June in the 13th year of the Republic, the accumulated debt owed over the years had reached more than 400,000 yuan. This year, in accordance with the steps of reorganizing local finance as resolved at the finance conference, all counties were convened to hold a financial small group meeting on issues such as reducing land tax surcharges, abolishing excessive taxes and miscellaneous levies, and reviewing general estimates. Regarding the land tax surcharge portion, 800,796 yuan was scheduled to be suspended upon expiration, 498,687 yuan had reduced tax rates, and 304,554 yuan was completely exempted, totaling 1,604,037 yuan. Regarding the tax portion, after investigation, there were 457 types involving excessive taxes and miscellaneous levies, with an amount of 247,511 yuan, all of which were scheduled to be abolished uniformly from November 1.

Anhui Province: Anhui Province is located in the center of the Yangtze River and is not a poor province. However, due to repeated banditry and natural disasters, finances are becoming increasingly depleted. Currently, the Department of Finance has reviewed and approved methods for reducing illegal taxes and levies and those not approved or not for urgent use, including more than 70 types of miscellaneous levies, amounting to 67,632 yuan, 286,891 yuan in land tax surcharges, and 117,347 yuan in miscellaneous tax surcharges, totaling more than 470,000 yuan. There are also more than 150 types where income is considered excessive and trivial, but the expenditure is still legitimate, totaling 283,997 yuan, which are also scheduled to be abolished within the end of this year after other compensation is found.

Jiangxi Province: Jiangxi Province did not establish a budget from the 18th year of the Republic onward. The 19th and 20th years had no budget. All financial revenue and expenditure were disorganized. The tax situation was complicated, and coupled with the disturbances of the Communist bandits, there was no source to open. Therefore, the principle of thrift was adopted, and the budget for the 21st, 22nd, and 23rd years was prepared based on income. For the past three years, it has been able to meet the budget. Regarding taxes, starting from the 13th year, the production tax on bamboo, wood, paper, summer cloth, medicinal materials, and oils was exempted first, totaling more than 500,000 yuan. Land tax surcharges were reduced by more than 3,100,000 yuan, and excessive taxes and miscellaneous levies were abolished by more than 1,200,000 yuan. At the same time, a legal business tax was planned, and the original bandit suppression and post-disaster donations were abolished.

Hunan Province: The finances of Hunan Province have been declining due to repeated bandit disasters and natural disasters. The revenue is insufficient, and the expenditure is huge due to the construction of highways and other unavoidable projects, resulting in increasing deficits. The provincial local budget for the 23rd year, with revenue and expenditure each totaling 14,087,543 yuan. Although the revenue and expenditure figures are suitable, the actual expenditure is definitely more than this number. In addition, the drought this year has made the revenue feel even more insufficient. After the resolutions of the Second National Finance Conference were promulgated, the Hunan Department of Finance immediately sought to reorganize them. Among them, local miscellaneous levies are the most burdensome, and the ones that cannot be completely abolished for a while are the two items of regimental defense and education. All miscellaneous levies total more than 50 types, with an annual income of 1.6 million, which has recently been abolished uniformly. Regarding land tax surcharges, it is planned to reduce the regimental defense surcharge by 8 jiao per tael, reducing 900,000 annually. As for the surcharges that still exceed the regular tax, it is planned to reduce them gradually over three years, reducing one-third each year. The temporary donations of various counties, townships, and towns have also been strictly prohibited. A total of 390,000 yuan has been reduced in counties such as Liling, Cichun, Rucheng, Xinhua, Dayong, Qiyang, Chenxian, and Hengshan.

Hubei Province: Hubei Province is located in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River, in a strategic location, and commerce is prosperous. Before the 20th year of the Republic, revenue and expenditure could be maintained. After the abolition of the Likin tax in the 21st year, revenue decreased sharply. In addition, the Communist disaster and floods made finances even more difficult, reducing 10,000 yuan to 18 million yuan. Starting this year, we will follow the order to abolish excessive taxes and miscellaneous levies. The first batch will abolish 27 types of old miscellaneous levies in Yichang, Shashi, Xindi, Wuxue, Laohekou, Fancheng Shayang, and other commercial ports, with a donation amount of 286,000 yuan, which will be abolished on July 1. In addition, 221 yuan was cut, and 62 types of miscellaneous tax items in 39 counties, including Puqi, were abolished, totaling 451,984 yuan. The Wuxue commercial port continued to abolish two types of donations from salt merchants and wharf donations, totaling 250 yuan. The above four items have jointly reduced more than 1,258,400 yuan. The remaining land tax surcharges exceed the regular tax, due to the need for funds or related to education, and those that cannot be abolished temporarily before compensation is obtained must also be reduced separately in accordance with the rules and within the time limit.

Henan Province: The finances of Henan Province have gradually gotten on track after repeated reorganizations. The annual revenue has increased from 5,283,694 yuan in the 19th year to 13,696,313 yuan. Various expenditures have been greatly reduced, and the comparison with the previous year has reduced a total of 2,535,671 yuan. Revenue and expenditure are sufficient to offset each other. However, due to the need to deal with river control, road construction, and rural revival, the expenditure is slightly difficult. Efforts are still being made to abolish excessive taxes and miscellaneous levies. More than 300 types of provincial and county miscellaneous levies have been abolished successively, and 46 types of land tax surcharges in various counties have been investigated and exempted. Now, we are also planning to continue to abolish (A) all existing miscellaneous levies in various counties, which are considered illegal or too excessive, a total of 32 types, totaling 264,572 yuan, to be abolished by the end of the year; (B) all deed tax surcharges in various counties that exceed half of the regular tax, totaling 234,915 yuan, to be abolished uniformly starting from the 24th year; (C) all types of donations and various taxes and levies that do not belong to the previous two items, totaling 352,019 yuan, are planned to be gradually cleaned up and abolished. (To be continued)

Politics Are on Track, Remaining Bandits Not Worthy of Concern

Compiled an Inspection Report and Returned to Jiangxi to Report

Hankou Dispatch: Jiang, Chairman of the Military Affairs Commission, previously dispatched Xu Qingyu, Director of the Party, Government, and Military Investigation Office of the Nanchang Headquarters, to Hunan and Hubei provinces to investigate the progress of Party affairs, politics, military affairs, and the New Life Movement, and to inquire about the people's hardships at any time, in order to carry out reforms. Xu has compiled a report on the inspection of Hunan and Hubei provinces and will submit it to Chairman Jiang for review. Xu told reporters today, in summary, that during the week-long inspection in Hubei, the military and political affairs were all managed by capable people, Party affairs also made progress, police services worked hard, and the achievements in the Wuchang area were particularly noteworthy. Currently, the remaining bandits in the entire territory have been suppressed, and the authorities' policy focus is on production and construction, which is indeed a good remedy for saving the situation. The New Life Movement is progressing smoothly, and there is a possibility that it will be designated as a model province for the New Life Movement in the future. In Hunan, he visited Changsha, Hengzhou, and Xiangtan. The Party, government, and military affairs have all made progress. In terms of Party affairs, cooperation between the two factions of Jia and Yi has been achieved, prejudices have been abandoned, and disputes have been resolved. In terms of politics, everything is on track. In terms of military affairs, southwest Hunan has gradually become calm. Since He Jian went to Baoqing to supervise the army, the morale has been boosted, and the gathering of central government reinforcements has posed a major threat to the remaining bandits. Currently, the two groups of He Long and Xiao Ke have fled to western Sichuan, and it will not be difficult for the two provinces of Hunan and Sichuan to join forces and wipe them out in one fell swoop. (25th)

The Depression of Jiujiang's Market 99

No Goods to Transport by Land or Water

A Glimmer of Hope for the Porcelain Industry

Jiujiang Correspondence: Jiangxi is an agricultural region along the Yangtze River. Before 1926, rice, porcelain, tea, summer cloth, paper, bamboo, wood, tungsten, and vegetable oils were exported in large quantities, with values often reaching millions. All were transferred through this port to various ports along the Yangtze River and sold both domestically and internationally. The major wharves and warehouses of Jiujiang were piled high with goods. Transfer stations, customs brokers, pawnshops, and various trade associations stood shoulder to shoulder, even surpassing Nanchang. Now, due to the impact of economic decline, all industries have declared bankruptcy. The Nanxun Railway, Jiangxi River boats, and Yangtze River steamers have almost no goods to transport, with only imports and no exports. Moreover, since the establishment of the Bandit Suppression and Rehabilitation Production and Sales Tax Bureau in Jiujiang the year before last, Jiujiang's already feeble commerce has been burdened with another layer of shackles. Although the production tax has been abolished this year, the elimination of the import surtax remains indefinitely postponed. To avoid this tax, merchants either transship goods through Wuxue to the upper reaches or Anqing to the lower reaches. Except for merchants from the provincial capital and the interior, most merchants from the border areas of the three provinces detour to avoid Jiujiang, causing the market to become even more depressed. However, in the past two years, Chairman Chiang Kai-shek has resided in Lushan and convened several important meetings, also transferring middle and upper-level military officers from across the country to Lushan for training in stages. As a result, the road to Xunyang and Lushan was crowded with officials and dignitaries, which significantly benefited the hotel and fine porcelain industries in Jiujiang, enabling them to break free from the atmosphere of economic downturn. To further revitalize the porcelain industry, the provincial government has specially established the Guangda Porcelain Company in Xunyang, with Du Chongyuan as the director. The scale is quite grand, and it may contribute to the prosperity of Xunyang in the future. (20th)

Strict Prohibition of Unauthorized Reclamation of the State-Operated Jinshui Farm 100

Nanchang Headquarters Cables Hubei Provincial Government

Instructing Local Authorities in Four Counties to Crack Down at Any Time

Hankou Correspondence: The Jinshui River basin in Hubei Province spans four counties: Wuchang, Jiayu, Puqi, and Xianning, covering an area of over one million mu. Over the years, it has been subject to backflow from the Yangtze River, turning into a marshland during the spring and summer seasons, leading to disasters. After the Three Provinces Bandit Suppression Headquarters, in consultation with the National Economic Council, raised substantial funds and built the Jinkou Sluice Dam, the accumulated waterlogged areas have been transformed into fertile land. Furthermore, the headquarters decided to trial-run a state-operated farm and established the "Preparatory Office for the State-Operated Jinshui River Basin Farm." Subsequently, Chen Zhenxian, the director of the Rural Revival Business Preparatory Office, was also assigned to handle this matter. On one hand, the headquarters issued a public announcement to clear public and private property rights and register them to prevent disputes. Before the completion of the clearing, private speculative buying and selling were invalid. The announcement was issued on March 7, and it has been nine months since then. Many residents have reclaimed wasteland by recruiting people without completing registration procedures, and the prohibition has been ineffective. Chen Zhenxian fears that this will hinder the state-operated enterprise and has submitted a request to the Nanchang Headquarters to take measures to crack down on it. After receiving the report, the headquarters cabled the Hubei Provincial Government yesterday, instructing the heads of counties, districts, bao, and jia to strictly prohibit it at any time, and also issued the following announcement: "According to the report submitted by Chen Zhenxian, the director of the Rural Revival Business Preparatory Office, this office previously received an order from your Excellency to take over the affairs of the Preparatory Office for the State-Operated Jinshui River Basin Farm. Following this order, personnel were dispatched to take over. It has been found that many people within the Jinshui River Basin area have not come to this office to apply for registration, and their property rights have not yet been determined. They have taken the dried-up lake wasteland and recruited people to reclaim it without authorization. The Preparatory Office for the State-Operated Jinshui River Basin Farm has already issued a public announcement prohibiting this. According to the report, more people have recently privately recruited people to reclaim land than before. If strict measures are not taken to prohibit it, it will greatly hinder the construction of the state-operated farm. It is proposed to issue a public announcement to prohibit it, ordering the Hubei Provincial Government to instruct the county magistrates of Wuchang, Jiayu, Puqi, and Xianning to instruct the heads of bao and jia in various districts of the Jinshui River Basin to effectively stop it at any time to facilitate progress, etc. After investigation, the households within the Jinshui River Basin area whose property rights to the dried-up lake wasteland have not yet been determined should be strictly prohibited from reclamation to prevent disputes and facilitate clearing. In addition to instructing the Hubei Provincial Government to instruct the county magistrates of Wuchang, Jiayu, Puqi, and Xianning to instruct the heads of bao and jia in various districts of the Jinshui River Basin to effectively stop it at any time, this announcement is hereby issued to all business households and others to comply with and not violate it." (23rd)

Guangdong Provincial Government Prepares to Establish a Textile Factory 101

Managers and Supervisors to be Appointed by the Provincial Government

The Guangdong Construction Department to Act as Supervisor

Guangzhou Correspondence: The Guangdong Provincial Government has recently been preparing to establish a textile factory to engage in the weaving of silk, wool, cotton, hemp, etc., to promote domestic goods and resist foreign imports. The factory's regulations have already been drafted and are being submitted to the provincial government for approval and filing. The internal organization of the factory is detailed in the regulations. The regulations are recorded below:

Article 1: The regulations for the organization of the Guangdong Textile Factory (hereinafter referred to as the Factory) are formulated in accordance with the provisions of Article 16 of the Revised Outline of the Guangdong Provincial State-Operated Industry Organization. Article 2: The Factory is subordinate to the Guangdong Provincial Government, with the Guangdong Construction Department as the supervisor, and engages in the weaving of silk, wool, cotton, hemp, and other materials. Article 3: The Factory shall have a manager who is responsible for all factory affairs and directs and supervises all employees under his jurisdiction. Article 4: The Factory shall have a supervisor who supervises all factory affairs. The rules for the supervisor's office shall be determined separately. Article 5: The Factory shall have departments for general affairs, silk weaving, silk making, wool spinning and weaving, silk hemp yarn, and cotton spinning and weaving, as well as an electrical engineering room. Each shall have a director who, under the manager's command, shall handle the affairs under their respective jurisdiction. Article 6: The General Affairs Department shall be responsible for the following matters: 1. Drafting, receiving, sending, sealing, managing files, and proofreading documents. 2. Registration of personnel appointments, dismissals, advancements, and retirements. 3. Custody of money, receipts, disbursements, bookkeeping, and the preparation of budgets and final accounts. 4. Statistics, summaries, and custody of contracts. 5. Preparation of other forms and schedules. 6. Procurement of miscellaneous items for the Factory. 7. Management and supervision of menial workers. 8. Compiling agendas and records for factory affairs meetings. 9. Protection of the Factory. 10. Medical services for the Factory. 11. Attendance records for technicians in each department. 12. Custody, receipt, dispatch, and registration of various raw materials, machine materials, and fuels. Article 7: The Silk Weaving Department shall be responsible for the following matters: 1. Production of silk warp and weft threads. 2. Production of silk fabrics. 3. Dyeing and refining of silk products. 4. Technical evaluation of technicians in the department and the production of daily, monthly, and manufacturing reports. Article 8: The Silk Making Department shall be responsible for the following matters: 1. Selection of cocoons. 2. Boiling of cocoons. 3. Silk making. 4. Packaging of silk products. 5. Technical evaluation of technicians in the department and the production of daily and monthly reports. Article 9: The Silk Hemp Yarn Department shall be responsible for the following matters: 1. Selection, allocation, refining, washing, and drying of silk hemp raw materials. 2. Spinning of silk hemp roving. 3. Spinning of fine yarn. 4. Spinning of thread yarn. 5. Finishing and inspecting finished products. 6. Inspection of silk hemp raw materials. 7. All other silk hemp manufacturing matters. Article 10: The Wool Spinning and Weaving Department shall be responsible for the following matters: 1. Combing and spinning of wool materials. 2. Machine weaving of wool materials. 3. Finishing of wool fabrics. 4. Technical evaluation of technicians in the department and the production of daily and monthly reports. Article 11: The Cotton Yarn Weaving Department shall be responsible for the following matters: 1. Pre-spinning of cotton silk fabrics. 2. Fine spinning of cotton yarn weaving. 3. Finishing and dyeing of cotton fabrics. 4. Technical evaluation of technicians in the department and the production of daily and monthly reports. Article 12: The Electrical Engineering Room shall be responsible for the following matters: 1. Electrical machinery repair. 2. Supply of electricity. 3. Reporting of daily and monthly reports. Article 13: Each department and room of the Factory may be divided into groups and sections to handle affairs according to the complexity of the work. Article 14: The Factory may have several technicians and technical assistants due to technical considerations, who, under the manager's command, assist the heads of each department in handling matters within their responsibilities. Article 15: Each department and group of the Factory may, as necessary for business, appoint several clerks. Article 16: The manager and supervisor of the Factory shall be appointed and dismissed by the Guangdong Provincial Government. The directors of each department, technical directors, and the chief accountant shall be appointed by the provincial government. Article 17: The Factory's procurement of all raw materials, machine parts, and fuels shall be handled by the Purchasing Committee. Article 18: In order to discuss the progress of factory affairs, the manager may periodically convene a factory affairs meeting composed of the heads of each department, section chiefs, group leaders, and technicians. Article 19: If there are any matters not covered in these organizational regulations, the manager may submit them to the Guangdong Construction Department, which will forward them to the Guangdong Provincial Government for approval and amendment. Article 20: The Factory's detailed rules of procedure shall be determined separately. Article 21: These regulations shall take effect from the date of approval and promulgation by the Guangdong Provincial Government.

Songjiang

Robbery of Villagers in Caojing Township 102

The home of Shen Menggen, a villager in Hutang Township, 31st Tu, Caojing, Punan, was suddenly attacked the other night by more than ten bandits speaking with a local accent. Armed with handguns and ropes, they broke down the front door and entered the house, barging into the bedroom and ransacking chests and cabinets, searching at will. They also severely injured the owner's mother, Shen Cai, and looted for an hour. They stole two pairs of gold earrings, more than ten pieces of clothing, and sacks, etc. After the robbery, the bandits left through the front door and fled south. The owner has reported the robbery to the 9th Precinct and requested that the stolen goods be recovered and the bandits apprehended.

Smuggling Ship Collides 103

The Nitre and Sulphur Bureau of this county, recognizing the widespread smuggling of nitre and sulphur in the surrounding villages, sent Chen Zhongjie and other inspectors the other day to hire a boat and proceed to the towns along the coast to conduct investigations. After inspecting Huangqiao Town, they continued to Sanjiaodu Sancheyang. Suddenly, a stone boat sailed from the east, driven by the wind. The crew of the patrol boat, seeing the dangerous approach, fearing a collision, urgently stopped the ship. The stone boat paid no attention, resulting in the two bows colliding. The patrol boat could not withstand the impact and tilted. Li Tingfu, an inspector on the patrol boat, was injured on the spot. All the passengers on board rushed to escape. The crew of the stone boat, fearing that the rescue of the patrol boat would be detrimental to them, continued sailing and avoided providing assistance. Fortunately, He Shimin, a crew member on the patrol boat, used a gun to stop them, and the seven members of the patrol boat were rescued onto the stone boat. They arrived at Chuanlai Temple Town, but the patrol boat had lost a box gun and other miscellaneous items, with losses exceeding 400 yuan.

Suzhou

Inspection Visit by the Director of the Security Department 104

Xiang Zhizhuang, the director of the Jiangsu Provincial Security Department, arrived in Suzhou yesterday (26th) from the province to inspect the county security team here. He is scheduled to convene a grand review of the security teams of all counties in Zhenjiang on New Year's Day. The security teams of Suzhou and Wuxi will be combined into one large team and will depart for Zhenjiang on the 29th to await inspection.

Complete Destruction of the Wenxin Company 105

The Wenxin Printing Company inside the Lumen, with a strong capital base and a large scale, was the leading printing company in Suzhou. Suddenly, at around 7 p.m. on the 25th, an electrical short circuit occurred in the machine room. In an instant, all the lights went out, and a fire broke out. More than 100 workers fled in panic in the dark. The fire brigade was notified and rushed to extinguish the fire, which was eventually put out. However, all 50 or so workshops were reduced to ashes, with losses estimated at over 100,000 yuan, including the buildings.

Wuxi

Land Sales and Transfers Must Be Registered 106

The household declarations of urban land prices in this county were concluded on the 15th of this month as scheduled. They are now being reviewed in preparation for public announcement. Once the announcement period has expired and no one has raised any objections, certificates will be issued as proof of ownership. However, owners may still engage in buying and selling after the land price declaration. These land changes must be registered with the declaration office to be valid. The land price declaration office issued a notice yesterday for all owners to be aware of. In addition, with regard to rights other than land ownership, including superficies, perpetual leasehold, easements, mortgages, and pledges, all people with the above rights should obtain a "Request for Rights Other Than Land Ownership" form from the land price declaration office within the announcement period and apply for registration in accordance with the regulations.

Gang Robbery of Rice at Lezhai Charity Estate 107

In Lezhai, near Anzhen in the 7th District of the county, there is a Huang family charity estate's rent collection point, which is managed by Huang Xilong. The houses are spacious, and when the tenants come to pay rent, they sleep together. Suddenly, more than 30 thugs resembling farmers broke down the door and entered the room, carrying away the accumulated rent rice in sacks on their shoulders. Back and forth they travelled, stealing over 50 shi of rough rice. Another group of people opened the money cabinet and took away 16 silver dollars and over 10,000 copper coins. At that time, the rent collector Bu Yongde was tied to a courtyard pillar after shouting loudly, and his clothes were also stripped off. The thugs then boarded an open boat that was moored at Zhujia Wharf and untied the ropes, leaving. Afterwards, the Public Security 8th Precinct of the town was notified and sent police to round them up. Five thugs who had not boarded the boat were apprehended, and the remaining ropes, flashlights, measuring tools, and buckets were taken to the precinct and then transferred to the Public Security Bureau for interrogation by the county. In addition, at the Zhenfeng Rice Store in Caiqiao, Ganlu Town, over 50 shi of white rice purchased by rice merchants were moored on the riverbank. At midnight, six burly men suddenly came with sharp blades, forcing the boatmen to row the boat to the Jialingdang Lake, about three li from the town, and stole all the rice. By the time the police were notified, the bandits had already fled far away.

Chongming

Scrape Salty Soil to Make Salt Trend 108

The people in the coastal areas of Chongming scrape salty soil and make salt. The tax police, thinking this affects tax revenue, have banned it. However, many people scrape and fry salt, and the ban is ineffective. The tax police opened fire, killing two people, which sparked a major disturbance. Local order is extremely chaotic. The county magistrate, Wang Bin, came to Tongzhou on the 25th to ask the 4th District Security Command to dispatch troops to suppress the unrest.

Haimen

Sudden Death of Education Bureau Clerk

Chen Guohua, clerk of the Education Bureau, a resident of Gaoqiao in the 1st District, was 25 years old. His wife, Ruan Yaqing, is the current principal of Gaoqiao County Primary School. The couple had a strong relationship. However, Chen, because of his poor family and insufficient income, was heavily in debt and unable to repay it, so he often had thoughts of ending his life. On the night of the 13th of last month, he took 20 sleeping pills at home, intending to commit suicide, but was discovered and rescued by his family. He was unharmed. The other day (23rd), Chen went to Gaoqiao Primary School to visit his wife. During their conversation, there was a slight disagreement, and Yaqing was unhappy and returned home alone. That night, Chen stayed at the school alone. Yesterday morning (24th), a school worker entered the room to sweep and saw Chen lying on the ground with him cold. The worker ran to inform his family, and they carried him home for burial. However, how he died, there are no clues to be found.

Robbery and Injury in Andong Township 109

The home of Xie Baomin, a farmer in Andong Township, 5th District, Qidong, was robbed on September 9 of this year, resulting in significant losses. A report was filed with the county government, ordering a strict investigation. It has not yet been solved. Unexpectedly, at around 10 p.m. the other day, more than ten bandits came again, each holding a box gun, and broke down the door. Xie, seeing the danger, fled through the back door, and was shot in the right arm by the bandits, who opened fire. He fell to the ground bleeding profusely. The bandits twisted Xie's wife, Shi, and forced her to hand over silver dollars, but failed. They beat her into injury and then ransacked chests and cabinets at will. After an hour, they left with a yell. After checking, the loss of silver dollars, ornaments, etc., was about 200 yuan. Xie lost too much blood and his injuries were very serious, fearing for his life.

Change of County Public Security Bureau Chief 110

Hao Zhiying, the chief of the County Public Security Bureau, has been in office for four years. He has worked hard in handling police affairs. However, due to improper use of personnel, there have been many malpractices. Recently, Ding Zuozhou, the chief inspector, was accused of taking illegal commissions and was dismissed. Wang Minghui, a detective, communicated with bandits and committed robberies, and was arrested on the spot. After interrogation by the county government, he was executed by shooting. Hao Zhendong, a patrol officer, manufactured and sold red pills and was arrested and detained by the special commissioner's office. As a result, Hao became uneasy in his position and submitted his resignation. The Civil Affairs Department has approved it, and Dai Hongtao has been appointed to fill the vacancy. After receiving the order, Director Hao instructed all officers to complete the handover yesterday. The new Director Dai, currently a section member of the Nantong District Commissioner's Office, is scheduled to come to Haimen on New Year's Day to take over the duties.

Zhenjiang

Full Opening of the Zhencheng Road 111

Zhenjiang Correspondence: The Zhencheng Highway, the main road from the provincial capital to Jiangyin, is 115 kilometers long and occupies a very important position in military affairs and transportation. Since the completion of the earth road, the Jiangsu Construction Department has been actively constructing the road surface in sections. In addition to the Wujin to Menghe and Zhenjiang to Jianbi sections which were opened for trial traffic on the 1st of last month, the entire section of the road surface has now been completely paved. The Jiangsu Provincial Highway Administration has scheduled a full opening today (26th) and will officially sell tickets starting today. No opening ceremony will be held for the time being. The area through which the road passes is densely populated with towns and cities, and the passenger traffic is extremely crowded. Over twenty long and short-distance bus trips are needed to accommodate the demand. The journey from the provincial capital to Jiangyin can be completed in just three to five hours. The Highway Administration also plans to set up a river ferry in Jiangyin, so that the counties downstream can use this shortcut to reach the ports of Nanjing and Shanghai. The journey will take no more than ten hours. The roads in southern Jiangsu are being completed one after another. Only the road surfaces of the Xihu (Wuxi to Shanghai) and Liwu (Lishui to Wujin) roads have not yet been constructed and are being actively planned. The Construction Department plans to convene a meeting in the coming days to prepare for the opening of all the highways in the province. It is expected to be around March of next year.

Nantong

Water Police Squadron Goes to Sea to Suppress Bandits 112

Chi Yaozong, the 3rd District Chief of the Jiangsu Provincial Water Police, came to Tongzhou and concentrated his squadron's ships at Lvsi. On the 25th, he went to sea to suppress sea bandits. The 13th and 14th Squadrons, and the pursuit squadron of the Provincial Security Team, took the front line, under the command of Qiu Xiangfeng. The 11th Squadron took the right wing, and the 12th Squadron took the left wing. Chief Chi was the commander-in-chief. The office was set up on a patrol boat, following the whole squadron forward. Currently, there are over 20 bandit ships and three or four hundred bandits occupying the waters of both North and South Kan, openly resisting. The bandit side also has a gasoline boat.

Gruesome Murder of Male Corpse Found East of Huoshaomiao 114

A gruesomely murdered male corpse was found the other day in a wasteland east of Huoshaomiao, bordering Baoying County to the north in Beihe Township, 8th District of this county. The upper body was naked, the lower body was wearing padded trousers, and the shoes and socks on his feet were intact. There were three wounds from a kitchen knife on his neck. There were even more knife wounds on his face, which was bloody and blurred, a very gruesome sight. A kitchen knife and over a zhang of paper money were found next to the body. The village constable has reported the case and is investigating the murderer.

City News

Ministry of Finance Strictly Investigates Rumors Disrupting the Market 115

Instructing the Silver and Money Trade Association

To Inform Members Not to Believe Lightly

Central News Agency reports that the authorities of the Ministry of Finance, due to the recent frequent spread of various rumors by villains attempting to disrupt the market and take advantage of the situation, have issued a special instruction to the Shanghai Banking Association and the Money Trade Association, ordering them to inform all members not to believe lightly and to strictly investigate the rumor-mongers for legal action. The original order is excerpted below for compliance: "It has recently been heard that villains are spreading rumors in the market, claiming that the government will centralize cash and implement inconvertible paper currency, or that it will reduce the fineness of currency and adopt an inflationary policy. These rumors are all speculative fabrications by villains attempting to disrupt the market and take advantage of the situation. The ignorant masses are misled by them and spread them, greatly affecting the market. It should be known that the government's measures are all based on national economy and people's livelihood, and there is no policy that is not in line with the current economic situation of our country. Therefore, it is hereby ordered that the Association immediately inform all members not to lightly believe rumors and disturb each other. For villains who deliberately spread rumors, they should be investigated and reported confidentially for investigation and to stabilize the market. This order."

Yu Youren Went to Beijing Yesterday 116

President of the Control Yuan, Yu Youren, came to Shanghai from Beijing on the 21st to seek medical treatment for his chronic illness. He has recovered in recent days, so he took the night express to Beijing last night.

French Ambassador to China, Weilitun, Visited Kong Yesterday 117

Discussing the Sino-Vietnamese Commercial Treaty

China United News Agency reports that the French Ambassador to China, Mr. Weilitun, accompanied by Counselor Dugluo and Chinese Secretary You Lifu, left Beijing for Shanghai the night before last and arrived at the port at 7 a.m. yesterday. He then went to the French Consulate to rest at the Ambassador's office. At around 10 a.m., he, accompanied by Counselor Dugluo and Secretary You Lifu, went to the Central Bank to meet with Mr. Kong Xiangxi. After a meeting of about an hour, he left and drove back to the French Consulate.

Meeting on the Commercial Treaty 118

A reporter from the China United News Agency went to the French Consulate to interview Mr. Dugluo after the French Ambassador met with Minister Kong. According to Dugluo, the visit with Minister Kong Xiangxi was to exchange views on the tariff rates in the Sino-Vietnamese Commercial Treaty. When asked by the reporter if the news from Beijing that the Sino-Vietnamese Commercial Treaty was about to be signed was true, Mr. Dugluo declined to comment.

Course of Consultations 119

The Sino-Vietnamese Commercial Treaty was first discussed with the French Ambassador Weilitun when Wang Zhengting was the Minister of Foreign Affairs, but was then suspended for various reasons. Therefore, the reporter then went to visit Mr. Wang, but failed to meet him because he was out. The reporter then visited a certain unofficial person who held an important position in the Ministry of Foreign Affairs at that time to inquire about the course of consultations at that time. According to the reply, the Sino-Vietnamese Commercial Treaty was revised in 1920 by the former Minister of Foreign Affairs, Wang Zhengting, and approved by our side. However, the French side has not yet approved it, so it cannot be implemented. Currently, the import of our goods is subject to ordinary import taxes, making it difficult to sell Chinese silk, tea, firecrackers, ceramics, hardware, groceries, and everything else. Therefore, overseas Chinese groups in Vietnam, the Yunnan Chamber of Commerce, and others have successively telegraphed the government, requesting the revision of the new treaty as soon as possible. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs then submitted the matter to the French side for further negotiations.

The Crux of the Problem 120

However, this issue is extremely complex, and the important crux is the Sino-Vietnamese border and tariff issues. Because the Sino-Vietnamese territorial sea and high seas fishing zones have not been demarcated for a long time, our fishing boats are often subject to harsh penalties. In early 1923, the authorities of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, due to the repeated requests of overseas Chinese merchants in Annam for negotiations, repeatedly negotiated with the French Ambassador Weilitun, but ultimately the two sides disagreed on the issue of reciprocal goods in the new treaty, and the dispute has not been resolved. As for tariffs, the French side also requested a reduction in the increased tax on imported foreign rice, which our country refused to agree to. Therefore, these two issues are the major crux of the prolonged failure to revise the treaty.

Resumption of Negotiations 121

When the French Ambassador Weilitun returned to his home country, he asked his government for instructions. On his return to China, he brought with him the instructions of the French government, so on the 13th of this month, he entered Beijing from Pingjin and reopened negotiations with the authorities of our Ministry of Foreign Affairs to continue consultations. Currently, the views of both sides are gradually converging, and it is expected that the commercial treaty will be signed soon after the beginning of the year.

Smooth Navigation on the Datong Waterway 123

Passengers and Cargo Embark and Disembark as Usual

Datong is an inland port on the Yangtze River. China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, Sanpei, Ning Shao, and other Chinese shipping companies all have branches established there, with ships moored for the loading and unloading of cargo and passengers from ships traveling up and down the Yangtze. When the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Jiang'an ship sailed downstream to Shanghai this time, it did not stop at Datong, for the sake of navigation safety. However, yesterday, various shipping companies received a telegram from the port stating that Datong is stable, its defenses are very secure, and Yangtze River ships can pass through as usual, with no obstacles to cargo transportation and passenger travel. Therefore, starting today, the Yangtze River ships will resume transporting cargo and passengers to Datong.

Zhengtai Railway's Yugu Branch Line Joins National Through Freight Transport 124

Three Stations: Xiuwen, Dongyangzhen, and Taigu County

To be Implemented Starting January 1st Next Year

The Bureau of the Two Railways (Pinghan and Zhengtai) received instructions yesterday from the Ministry of Railways stating that the Zhengtai Railway Bureau reported: "The Yugu branch line of this Bureau is located in a strategic area in southern Shanxi, and the stations along the line are becoming increasingly prosperous. To facilitate passengers and merchants and to expand business, it is proposed to include Xiuwen, Dongyangzhen, and Taigu County stations in the national railway through freight transport system starting January 1, 24th year of the Republic (1935). Full carload shipments for which the shipper is responsible will also be handled simultaneously, and Taigu County will be opened as a passenger through transport station. Parcel freight charges will be collected on behalf of other stations. Please examine and approve, and instruct all national through transport lines to take note and implement accordingly." It should be approved and implemented. In addition to instructing the Through Transport Department to expedite the compilation and distribution of passenger and freight kilometer rates between Shijiazhuang and these stations for use by all lines, and issuing separate orders, it is hereby urgently ordered that it be reported in accordance with the above and be widely publicized. This order has been relayed by the Bureau to the Traffic Department for compliance.

Qianye Trade Leader Qin Runqing Negotiates with Banking Syndicate Yesterday 125

One Million in Silver to be Released

*Shen Shi News Agency* Local News: Since the implementation of the U.S. silver purchase policy, silver has been flowing out of our country continuously. From January to November of this year, silver exports exceeded imports by over 250 million yuan. As of last week, the silver reserves of Chinese and foreign banks were only 300 million yuan (280 million yuan, 28.9 million taels), resulting in a widespread shortage of silver, which has further hindered the development of industry and commerce. Therefore, Qin Runqing, a leader in the Qianye trade, has carefully considered and planned a solution to the current stalemate. He specifically consulted with Chen Xing, Vice President of the Central Bank; Zhang Gongquan, General Manager of the Bank of China; and Tang Shoumin, General Manager of the Bank of Communications, to release 10 million yuan in silver to various Qian Zhuang (native banks), which would then provide loans to industrial and commercial circles with collateral. An increase in silver in the market would naturally stabilize confidence, and those who hoard silver due to rumors would release it. Silver circulation in the market would inevitably become more active, and the reserves of the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications would also be replenished through the release. This matter has been discussed and planned by Qin Runqing, Zhang Gongquan, and others at the Central Bank in several meetings, and last night, another meeting was held at Tang Shoumin's residence at the Bank of Communications. The results were very satisfactory. The reporter of *Shen Shi News Agency* has learned that the results of the meeting can be generally summarized as follows: (1) The Bank of China and the Bank of Communications will each release 4 million yuan, and the Central Bank will release 2 million yuan, for a total of 10 million yuan. (2) The interest rate for the release will be temporarily set at 7%. (3) Qian Zhuang in need of cash can separately contact the three banks to negotiate the release. If the need is greater, it may exceed 10 million yuan. However, according to observations in the financial sector, although the silver situation seems urgent, due to the decline in industry and commerce, the demand is not very high, and the 10 million yuan may not be fully utilized.

North China Private Goods Imported Tax Evasion Causes Significant Losses to Customs 126

Artificial Silk and White Sugar are Major Items

Stricter Patrols Have Slightly Reduced This Year

Along the coast of North China, there is a prevalent "junk trade," where large sand boats are used to secretly import tax-evading private goods. Those engaged in this trade are mostly unscrupulous merchants who collude with merchants from a certain country, with Dalian as the center. Each year, private goods worth several tens of millions of yuan are secretly transported from Dalian to various commercial ports in North China. The huge losses to our country's customs revenue can be imagined. According to a survey by a commercial organization operating in North China, since January of this year, in order to strictly prohibit smuggling, our country's customs has specifically dispatched customs cruisers to Tianjin, Zhifu, Weihaiwei, and Qingdao to strengthen patrols. As a result, up to now, a total of more than 180 sand boats carrying smuggled inferior goods have been intercepted, with a value of approximately 1.4 million yuan. Although secret imports have decreased compared to previous years, the total for this year is still around 13 million yuan. The smuggled goods are mainly artificial silk, accounting for the largest share. Apart from white sugar, amounting to 2.67 million yuan, the remaining 10 million yuan is mostly artificial silk. However, if North China Customs can continue to enforce strict patrols, the trend of smuggling will likely be greatly reduced in the future.

Participation in the Philippine Carnival Postponed Temporarily for One Year 131

Fundraising Halted, Preparatory Committee Issues Statement

The participation of Chinese national products in the Philippine Carnival was postponed yesterday (26th) when the seventh preparatory committee meeting was convened temporarily due to difficulties reported via telegram from the Philippines. Committee members, including Guo Shun, Hu Xiyuan, Fang Yexian, Qian Chengxu, Wang Hanqiang, Wang Jiean, Ye Hongcheng, Wu Zhihao, and Chen Yiting, elected Guo Shun as chairman. Regarding the Philippine conference, it was decided to postpone it for one year according to the Mayor's wishes. Regarding the fundraising portion, an urgent notice has been issued to all fundraising committee members to stop fundraising. Preparatory Committee Chairman and Vice-Chairman Guo Shun and Hu Xiyuan issued a statement saying that the preparatory committee, initiated and organized by Shanghai Mayor Wu Tiecheng, has been in operation for one month. Six committee meetings have been held during the preparation process, passing the organizational charter and product rules, and various participation procedures. The preparation is basically complete. As for the manufacturers, two fundraising conferences have been held, with more than 50 manufacturers participating. As for the financial aspect, the 10,000 yuan subsidy from the municipal government and the 10,000 yuan from the Executive Yuan have also been approved and can be claimed at any time. Such progress in a short period of time is due to the fact that personnel, credit, economic, and all other aspects are proceeding under favorable conditions, so the driving force is great. At the same time, everyone has worked diligently to promote it. On the 25th of this month, we received instructions from the Mayor, who said that he had received a telegram from Luzon, stating that the meeting had decided to cancel the display of goods exhibition because the cost to the factories and shipping companies was too great, and the local preparations could not be completed in time. The committee was asked for its opinion. The committee believes that it was ordered to prepare at that time, and from the committee's perspective, it is willing to set its steps under the Mayor's guidance. After deliberation, it was proposed that the preparatory committee should continue as before, and all the products that have already been solicited will be moved to February 1, 1936, for participation in the display, so that the time can be sufficient and the quantity of products collected can be increased. Postponement is the best option. However, whether this is the case, a committee meeting was convened to determine its policy. After the meeting, the reporter of this newspaper asked Qian Chengxu, Secretary-General of the committee, about the reason for the suspension. He replied that it is well known that Chinese national products have been subject to exclusion everywhere overseas in recent years. The preparatory procedures for this Philippine Carnival have been 60% completed, and yet for this reason, we cannot participate as scheduled, which causes endless thoughts. Regarding this section, I very much hope that our national government can take the protection of industry as a prerequisite everywhere, and that Chinese manufacturers can do their best to reorganize their factories, so that after more than a year, national strength will be sufficient, and the environment will naturally change. In short, the problem with this suspension is not in China, but in the Philippines.

Joint Transportation Contract and Water Transportation Fees between China Merchants Steam Navigation Company and Beining Railway 140

Regarding the joint land and water transportation matters handled by the state-owned China Merchants Steam Navigation Company and the Beining Railway, Director Zhou Fengtu of the company's Joint Transportation Group had already discussed the details with the authorities of the Beining Railway during his visit to Tianjin. The details were then submitted to the Ministry of Railways for approval. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company proposed Tianjin as the joint transportation station, which would allow the abundant products from provinces such as Hebei and Suiyuan to be transported to Shanghai, Guangdong, and other ports by the most convenient route. However, the Ministry of Railways, considering the freight business of the Jinpu Railway, proposed Bengbu as the joint transportation station, so that all goods would be transferred through the Jinpu Railway to avoid affecting its freight business. Therefore, the Ministry of Railways is still considering this matter and has not yet approved it. However, the joint transportation contract and freight rates have already been agreed upon. Once the Ministry of Railways approves, it can be implemented. It is said that one of the two ports, Tianjin and Bengbu, will be selected as the joint transportation station.

China National Aviation Corporation (CNAC) Purchases Streamlined, Silent Aircraft for the Shanghai-Beiping Route 142

Able to sing and broadcast at will inside the aircraft during flight

To be transported to Shanghai next month to improve the Shanghai-Beiping air route

To improve the Shanghai-Beiping air route, the China National Aviation Corporation (CNAC) recently ordered a new-style, large Douglas aircraft from the United States. The aircraft is expected to arrive in Shanghai next month for installation and application. According to reporters from Shen Shi News Agency who inquired at CNAC, the aircraft will be the only civilian aircraft in China with complete facilities. The design is the latest "streamlined" type, identical to the aircraft that won second prize in the England-Australia long-distance flight competition. Its external structure is similar to the "Boeing" aircraft recently purchased by Deputy Commander Zhang Xueliang. The aircraft can accommodate 14 passengers and is equipped with two engines and extremely modern facilities, including the "silent interior" feature. Because ordinary aircraft emit a high level of noise from the engine and the rotating propeller during flight, which is uncomfortable for passengers, the aircraft is equipped with a noise-canceling device. Passengers inside the cabin will not be disturbed by external noise during flight. Even during takeoff and landing, passengers will hardly notice it. Therefore, passengers can talk, sing, and even connect wireless and phonograph equipment inside the aircraft to entertain themselves during the lonely journey. Furthermore, the speed of the aircraft will be higher than that of ordinary civilian aircraft, with a normal speed of approximately 190 miles per hour. When ascending to an altitude of 80 feet or higher, the speed can increase to over 210 miles per hour. Therefore, after the aircraft is transported to Shanghai next year and added to the Beiping-Shanghai route, the flight time will be shortened.

Both Railway Administrations Issue Circular on Order and Cleanliness 143

The Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administrations issued a circular to all departments stating that by the end of this year, all departments of the Bureau and the North Shanghai and South Shanghai stations must achieve complete order and cleanliness. Regarding official duties, no official matters should be delayed, and files must be cleared. Regarding the office location, whether indoors or outdoors, down to every table and chair, everything must be thoroughly cleaned. Regarding individuals, clothing and appearance should also be noted. The Bureau will send personnel to inspect each of the above items separately by the end of this month to check the results. Therefore, all departments should be notified and instruct their subordinates to comply. This is the order.

Daylight Robbery at Hengyuanxiang Store: Bullets Fly, Passersby Flee in Terror 145

Cash Box Empty, Robbers Disappointed

Two Robbers Shot, Captured One After Another

The Hengyuanxiang Fabric Store, located at No. 20 Dongtingshan Alley, Doushi Street, outside the South City's Dadongmen, is owned by local Mu Shaoqin. However, the store has recently been struggling with poor business and financial difficulties and is in the process of liquidation. Unexpectedly, at around 11:00 AM yesterday, five robbers, dressed in various styles, entered the store under the pretext of searching for morphine. They pulled out guns and ordered everyone to be silent. They first drove everyone in the store into a corner and then opened the cash box, intending to loot it. However, the box was empty, and they were greatly disappointed. At that time, a female neighbor of the store discovered what was happening and opened the window to shout for help. In an instant, police sirens were heard everywhere. Hearing the sound, the five robbers realized that their plan had failed and gave a prearranged signal. They rushed out the door to escape. Soon after, four of the robbers fled to Yuelai Street, where they were heard by police officer Cheng Hong from the Langjia Bridge police post. He blew his whistle and gave chase. At this time, two of the robbers each took out a pistol and returned fire at Cheng, who pulled out his own gun and returned fire. At the same time, Wang Yulong from the 20th Post security watch and patrol police chief Dong Huatang arrived after hearing the alarm to assist in the arrest. Gunfire erupted on Yuelai Street, bullets flew, and passersby fled in terror, causing great disorder. As a result, more than 30 shots were fired by both sides. One of the robbers, named Wang Licheng, was shot in the right foot by the police and fell to the ground in pain at the entrance of Wujia Alley, where he was apprehended. A six-inch Browning pistol and one bullet were seized from him. He was then taken to the 16th Precinct Police Station. Later, Wang Songling, a security watchman from the 21st Post, received a report from a passerby that another robber, named Wang Youcai, had been found at the Xianzhua Street entrance in the Damatou area. His left foot had been shot and the bullet had not yet exited, and fresh blood was flowing. He was immediately taken to the precinct police station for investigation. The remaining three robbers who escaped are currently being pursued by the police.

During the interrogation, neither of the plaintiffs nor their attorneys appeared. Only the defendant, Lu Yaoming, appeared with his attorney, Yuan Yang'an. Attorney Yuan stated that the defendant was filing a counterclaim against the two plaintiffs, Wang Xingsheng and Wang Xingnan, for false accusation. After investigation, it was found that the plaintiffs were not students of Datong School. When investigating the letter sent to Zhangjia Alley, Baoce West Gate, no such person was found. The second letter, sent from No. 407 Baoshan Road, Shanghai, damaged the reputation of Datong. After the defendant reported this to the Shanghai Public Security Bureau, it was found that Wang Xingnan was working at the Chengxin Bank Correspondence School in the Zhonghui Building. After reporting to the French Concession Police, Wang Xingnan was arrested. Hu Zijun and Hu Wenbin, witnesses living with Wang Xingsheng, testified that Wang Xingsheng was instructed by Xi Yuehan, the principal of Chengxin School, to expand the organization and damage the reputation of Datong. They were then sent to the Second Special Court of Shanghai. The Baoshan County Government case files were investigated, and Wang Xingnan was ordered to post bail. Wang Xingsheng and others had also filed a complaint against the defendant in the Shanghai Education Bureau with the same facts. The Bureau also investigated and determined that they were not students of Datong School and were instigated by others to make false accusations. Therefore, the court was requested to write to the Education Bureau to investigate the circumstances and background of the case so that the truth could be revealed. Since the plaintiffs were not Datong students, they first made false accusations to the Education Bureau, and they should not be allowed to escape justice. Now they are making false accusations to this court, and they have not appeared today. A warrant should be issued for their arrest to clarify the truth. The judge adjourned the case to 2:00 PM on January 8, 1935, to summon the plaintiffs for further questioning.

Hazy Morning in Shanghai Yesterday 146

The weather in Shanghai has been mild for the past week, with temperatures consistently between 50 and 60 degrees Fahrenheit. There has also been heavy fog every day, which does not dissipate even during the day. Yesterday was particularly bad. It was impossible to distinguish between men and women ten zhang away. Around 8:45 AM, it suddenly became extremely dark, lasting for about 15 minutes. It was impossible to see indoors without turning on electric lights. The whole day was drizzly and extremely humid, making it unbearably oppressive, like the plum rain season. According to general expectations, the period of great cold is not far away, and it may snow.
